The code is trying to handle a specific type of deserialization error, but there's a flaw in the logic:\n\n1. When `deserialize_from_file()` raises a `ValueError` with the message \"DeserializationError\", it's caught and handled gracefully (lines 216-222).\n2. But that means any actual deserialization error with a different message will be re-raised and crash the application.\n\nLooking at the code flow:\n- Line 215: `self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))` \n\n\n- Line 216-217: If a ValueError is caught, the code checks if the error message is \"DeserializationError\"\n- Line 220: If it's NOT \"DeserializationError\", the exception gets re-raised, crashing the app\n\nThe logic is inverted—it only suppresses one specific error message and propagates everything else, which is what's causing the crash. The code checks `if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\": raise`, meaning it only suppresses the error when the message exactly matches that string. Any other ValueError gets re-raised, which is problematic because the error message from the Rust library might not be exactly \"DeserializationError\" - it could have additional context or formatting that causes the condition to fail and the exception to propagate unexpectedly. Any other ValueError gets re-raised, which would crash the application. Looking back at the braveadblock.py code, the problem in `read_cache()` is:\n\n```python\ndef read_cache(self) -> None:\n    \"\"\"Initialize the adblocking engine from cache file.\"\"\"\n    try:\n        cache_exists = self._cache_path.is_file()\n    except OSError:\n        logger.error(\"Failed to read adblock cache\", exc_info=True)\n        return\n\n    if cache_exists:\n        logger.debug(\"Loading cached adblock data: %s\", self._cache_path)\n        try:\n            self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\n        except ValueError as e:\n            if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n                # All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by\n                # python-adblock\n                raise\n            message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                          \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\nThe bug is on line 217: `if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":`\n\nThis checks if the string representation of the exception is exactly equal to \"DeserializationError\". If it's NOT equal, it re-raises the exception.\n\nHowever, based on the comment, all Rust exceptions from python-adblock are converted to ValueError. The actual error message might be something like \"DeserializationError\" or it might be formatted differently.\n\nThe real issue is that the condition is checking the wrong thing. It should probably be catching ALL ValueError exceptions from deserialize_from_file as deserialization errors, or it should be checking if the error message CONTAINS \"DeserializationError\" rather than being exactly equal to it.\n\nLet me think about what the actual error would be when you try to deserialize a corrupted file:\n\n1. If the python-adblock library raises an exception for a corrupted file, it would be a ValueError\n\n\n2. The error message might not be exactly \"DeserializationError\" - it could be \"Deserialization failed\" or some other variant\n3. The current logic re-raises any ValueError whose message doesn't match exactly, which means legitimate deserialization errors get propagated instead of being handled gracefully\n\nFor my regression test, I need to create a corrupted cache file that triggers a ValueError when deserialized, then verify the code handles it properly by showing the error message instead of crashing.\n\nTo corrupt the cache file, I could write garbage data, truncated content, or modified valid data - anything that breaks the deserialization process. The python-adblock library should fail when trying to parse malformed cache data.\n\nI'll assume deserialize_from_file raises a ValueError when it encounters corruption. For the test, I need to create a scenario where read_cache() receives corrupted data and the exception propagates unhandled, demonstrating the bug. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01SsPQfuJkNWkFH8WAngAoW4","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! Now I understand the issue completely. Looking at the code in braveadblock.py:\n\n```python\ntry:\n    self._engine.deserialize_from_file(str(self._cache_path))\nexcept ValueError as e:\n    if str(e) != \"DeserializationError\":\n        # All Rust exceptions get turned into a ValueError by python-adblock\n        raise\n    message.error(\"Reading adblock filter data failed (corrupted data?). \"\n                  \"Please run :adblock-update.\")\n```\n\nThe code is catching `ValueError`, but the actual exception raised by python-adblock is `adblock.DeserializationError`, which inherits from `adblock.BlockerException`, NOT `ValueError`!\n\nSo the exception is never caught by the `except ValueError` clause, and it propagates up as an unhandled exception, causing the application to crash.\n\nThis is the bug! The code should be catching `adblock.DeserializationError` (or more broadly, any adblock exception) instead of `ValueError`.\n\nNow I need to write a regression test that demonstrates this bug. When `deserialize_from_file()` encounters corrupted cache data, it raises `adblock.DeserializationError`\n2. The code attempts to catch `ValueError`, but `adblock.DeserializationError` inherits from `adblock.BlockerException`, NOT `ValueError`\n3. Because the exception type doesn't match, it is not caught by the `except ValueError` clause\n4. The exception propagates up as unhandled, causing the application to crash\n\n### Root Cause Details\nThe exception hierarchy is:\n```\nadblock.DeserializationError -> adblock.BlockerException -> Exception\n  (NOT a ValueError)\n```\n\nTherefore, the `except ValueError` handler will never catch `adblock.DeserializationError`, regardless of the error message check.\n\n## Expected Behavior\nThe application should:\n1. Detect the corrupted cache file\n2. Catch the deserialization error\n3. Display an error message to the user\n4. Continue running normally (allowing the user to browse without ad-blocking until the cache is rebuilt)\n\n## Actual Behavior\nThe application crashes with an unhandled `adblock.DeserializationError` exception before the browser window appears.\n\n## Test Case\nThe regression test in `/workspace/regression_test.py` demonstrates this bug:\n\n1. **test_corrupted_cache_file_raises_unhandled_exception**: \n   - Creates a BraveAdBlocker instance\n   - Creates a corrupted cache file with invalid data\n   - Calls `read_cache()` which raises `adblock.DeserializationError`\n   - Test FAILS on buggy code (exception is not caught)\n   - Test PASSES on fixed code (exception is caught and handled)\n\n2. **test_corrupted_cache_file_logs_error_message_after_fix**:\n   - Similar to above, but also verifies that `message.error()` is called\n   - Test FAILS on buggy code (exception is not caught)\n   - Test PASSES on fixed code (exception is caught and error message is shown)\n\n3. **test_valid_cache_file_loads_successfully**:\n   - Verifies that valid cache files still load correctly\n   - Test PASSES on both buggy and fixed code\n\n## How to Fix\nThe `except ValueError` clause should be changed to `except adblock.DeserializationError` (or more broadly, `except Exception` to handle all adblock-related exceptions).\n\nAfter the fix, the exception will be properly caught, the error message will be displayed to the user, and the application will continue running.\nEOF\ncat /workspace/BUG_ANALYSIS.md\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":482,"cache_read_input_tokens":52470,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":482},"output_tokens":6,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"eb0b96e5-26a0-488a-825c-12fa366337d7","uuid":"b77722cf-4d8a-419f-8f4f-00938087efd5"}
